commit e6051ad1684dfaa021a101be5a9089d3d7091c97
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Mon Mar 10 19:22:49 2025 +0100

    Prevent allocation of 0-size arrays in CvPlayerAI
    
    Allocating and freeing 0-size arrays is safe, but accesses in between are undefined behavior, so this is better avoided. It's also unnecessary, inconsistent with the pattern used in CvPlayer::reset and therefore likely accidental. BtS introduced this minor issue. [advc.001]
    
    I had temporarily added an assertion to the (preprocessor-generated) GC.getNum...Infos functions in order to check for any potential problems resulting from their use prior to XML loading. No issues found other than this one. (Then I also temporarily activated the internal memory manager and checked for zero memory allocations that way. Nothing else found that way either.)

commit 6fe41cc646c86fc69483d2edcd169000df9fadbc
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Feb 21 16:24:24 2025 +0100

    Apply AI improvement personality weights additively
    
    My previous method was still flawed and may have contributed to oscillation problems. Now the AI takes the personality weight times a scale factor and adds the result to the comparison value of the improvement yields (comparing one improvement under consideration with the one currently present in the tile). As the scale factor, I use the smallest of the yield priority values, so that a 100% personality weight will usually mean treating an improvement as if it granted one extra commerce. The actual weights in XML are a good deal smaller than 100% (currently either 20% or 30%). [advc.131, advc.005a]

commit 6c32e20f24623259477fa5620b5b5a9536b49979
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Feb 20 20:10:48 2025 +0100

    Reinforce K-Mod AI food priority correction (anti-oscillation)
    
    I don't think performance would be a big obstacle for addressing this problem more thoroughly, but I don't want to have to take apart the AI food target calculations, and I also doubt that this will ultimately make oscillating improvements much less common. I suspect that it's mainly a lack of AI workers that keeps this phenomenon rare one way or another.
    
    I've tweaked the correction coefficient by comparing actual and corrected AI food priority values both before and after placing a new improvement. The more pronounced correction still always seems to fall short of restoring the earlier food priority. To avoid oscillation, additional food should appear no more or less desirable to the AI only because it has just replaced an improvement (and now has more or less food available). But the numbers I've seen may reflect other changes too that happen in between turns. I think my tweak is still conservative; wouldn't want the AI to become inert about growing cities that need growth. I guess the correction also needs to make up for AdvCiv tweaks from years ago that make the AI more aggressive at growing cities. [advc.121]
    
    This CFC post prompted me to look into this (I think I'll also write a reply later):
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/ai-city-placement-and-misc-suggestions.695343/post-16779312

commit 9f04ec018c0b8a4f5e8fed3659239cc99ec41757
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Feb 20 19:55:02 2025 +0100

    Cleaner handling of discover chance in AI improv. eval.
    
    This way, existing Mines are treated as having a baseline value of 0, the same as any/most(?) other existing improvement that the AI considers to replace, and therefore should not be affected by the "improve better tiles first" logic. I'm not enthusiastic about the whole approach of evaluating differences from the current improvement (rather than the difference from a hypothetical unimproved tile - or more ambitiously the city's total yields), but it should at least be a little more consistent this way. [advc.121]

commit 154ae6bd22ecee96adc06faa525d23dc4c546325
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Jan 26 13:05:41 2025 +0100

    Cancel random event popup if trigger conditions no longer met
    
    Random events trigger at the end of a player's turn. If that player is human, the choice how to handle the event won't happen until the start of the player's next turn (via a popup). By then, the event may no longer make sense. So I'm now re-checking the trigger conditions before showing the popup. [advc.001]
    
    It might be that this approach won't work for certain events, e.g. if an event could only trigger, say, in a leap year. My best bet is to investigate any canceled events for a while; so I've left an assertion to that end in place. Getting popups to launch during AI Auto Play seems challenging, so this will really have to be tested with a human player in charge.
    
    This CFC thread made me aware of the delay between event trigger and popup:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/forced-to-provide-a-resource-brothers-in-faith-at-war.693778/

commit aa6bef8e31b031eaa43b7dcd330af7104daf0e1a
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Jan 10 20:30:38 2025 +0100

    AI war-declaring moves anticipate loss of Open Borders
    
    That is, the pathfinder no longer assumes that routes of a war target can be used when moving toward one of the target's cities. Impact on performance not measured, hopefully negligible given how complex the actual movementCost function is; checking the DoW check beforehand shouldn't move the dial.
    
    This change should make it much less likely that the path changes upon declaring war. In particular, the (already rare) phenomenon of an AI war declaration that is not immediately followed by units crossing the border will now, hopefully, be exceedingly rare. [advc.001t] (Also attaching that change id to a similar change previously covered by advc.082.)

commit 8d14920f7dddfdbc18110ed8238c70b398b0231c
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Jan 10 20:20:20 2025 +0100

    More reliable can-bombard checks in AI code
    
    Now always checks the whole group for units that can bombard a city, not just the unit leading the group. This faster approach may have been OK (likely not always optimal) in the base game, but, since then, BtS and AI mods have added code that expects a group to be able to bombard if any unit in it has that ability. One result of those inconsistencies were rare "blockage" problems in K-Mod code. These can-bombard checks don't get executed extremely frequently, I think; should not really be a performance concern. Repurposing change id advc.001j for these changes (freed up by the parent commit).

commit 704fb027a33a8078bbfcca0694bedc0ce3882fde
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Dec 11 22:23:17 2024 +0100

    Ensure that disabled map script options have no impact
    
    When the climate or sea level option is disabled, I set the map's climate to Temperate and sea level to Normal in case that different settings were carried over from the previously used map script. This ensures that disabled options don't affect the map generation process and also prevents them from affecting game rules and AI behavior. Through change advc.910, for example, research costs are affected by the sea level in AdvCiv. [advc.194]
    
    Prompted by this CFC post (note - I'm not sure if Arboria maps are really affected by climate or sea level):
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/taurus.677586/page-4#post-16616358

commit cd4282f9fb8bf792a353e416fdfc5abf4fae0f3d
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Oct 27 09:36:48 2024 +0100

    Espionage cost breakdown warns when civic/religion not practised
    
    When asked to choose a civic or religion for the change-civics or convert-religion espionage mission, the mission cost breakdown says that the cost is increased when the spy owner does not practise the civic or religion. It doesn't say by how much exactly because the calculation is rather complicated and the intention is just to make the spy owner aware that their own civics/ religion affect the cost and, more importantly, that the ability to choose civics and religions other than their own is a deliberate change in AdvCiv and not a bug. [advc.132]
    
    Related CFC post:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/advanced-civ.614217/post-16695294

commit 791a45ea07b51d153832d8b34474dd2ec88f1114
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Jul 4 16:09:36 2024 +0200

    Make AI_isControlled nonvirtual (for speed)
    
    I had kept a single CvSelectionGroup function pure virtual so that the class is abstract, which still seems reasonable to me, but I shouldn't have picked such a frequently called function. Rather than add a lot of (wrapper-enclosed) casts to CvSelectionGroupAI, I've moved the function to the base class, where it imo makes more sense anyway. And "AI_isControlled" was a silly name; now "isAIControlled". [advc.003u]
    
    Doing this also with the latest pathfinder tweak in mind; I think that will make AI-control checks a lot more frequent. [advc.pf]
    
    With both changes in place, the performance seems to be essentially unchanged based on a few measurements I've run. Which is fine with me.

commit b3de867844ccdf0937797e6a6375e22816d042f6
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Jul 4 15:38:00 2024 +0200

    Fix danger avoidance checks in pathfinder
    
    [advc.pf, advc.001]
    
    See commit 2eddf22d1761aa426ebe581908a3143069ce542c for context. I've convinced myself through AI Auto Play and comparisons with the original K-Mod pathfinder that my implementation is correct, i.e. at least strictly more correct than before. The use of path data in the cost function may still be a problem; hopefully one that will at worst lead to slightly suboptimal paths - and won't lead to inconsistencies between CvUnitAI and CvSelectionGroup that result in infinite loops.
    
    My tests suggest that, previously, suboptimal paths were generated several times per game, always for worker moves. Not very relevant so long as the game doesn't get stuck in a loop, which had been happening very rarely (and was caught by error-handling code).
    
    Performance still to be tested; I may yet revert this commit. But I think the effect will be negligible.

commit 8bfa61dfd7fc7f43b47519a34ac893066517907d
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Mar 23 22:22:52 2024 +0100

    Work around messages missed at the end of Hotseat turns
    
    [change id advc.106b]
    
    Works around a BtS issue: Messages triggered at the end of a human turn had been immediately cleared (having been displayed for only a split second, if at all) due to the next human player becoming active. Previously, AdvCiv had addressed this problem by opening the Turn Log at the start of every human turn - if the option for opening the Turn automatically was enabled at all. Now the auto-opening of the Turn Log should work the same way as in singleplayer mode, i.e. based on the message limit configured on the BUG menu.
    
    The missed messages are now repeated at the start of the recipient's next turn. Hopefully I'm successfully identifying exactly the right messages; otherwise, some will still be missed (only show up in the Turn Log) or some will appear twice. I did do some testing and tweaking.

commit d5d51b2513fd8935296a6218a3895686262776d4
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Mar 23 22:12:06 2024 +0100

    Fix repeated city-related Civ4lerts in Hotseat
    
    Turns out that some of the alerts in the original Civ4lerts module also need to store separate data for each human player, not just the MoreCiv4lerts, which I had already revised some years ago. Not surprising, really. The alert about a city having become unhappy, for example, was being repeated turn after turn. [advc.135b]

    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/realism-invictus.411799/post-16511367

commit 14e70f65350ac2f090d20738d0258b25c4420be4
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Jun 23 00:15:55 2023 +0200

    Border spread at edge of Fog of War can trigger meeting
    
    This change concerns a rare special case: Borders of an unmet rival spreading onto a fogged tile that is adjacent to a visible tile. In that case, the game will show the borders on the (whole) fogged tile (I guess so that the borders can then bleed onto the adjacent visible tile as they normally do), but no meeting occurs. I found this confusing, so a revealed tile (fully revealed but fogged) will now trigger a meeting if its owner becomes known. [advc.071b]

commit ce6a48ef0153b4d9c456fe19c4d5bff023f69ffa
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Jan 3 23:40:14 2023 +0100

    Tweak UWAI eval of 3rd-party interventions a bit more

commit 67383d167967b8a9ad34f84d1210a5c6afea064f
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Mon Jan 2 01:05:58 2023 +0100

    Tweak fear of 3rd-party interventions, esp. on crowded maps.
    
    UWAI was reducing war utility way too much in the early game on large, overcrowded continents for fear of 3rd-party interventions. I think the biggest issue was how the power ratio at the time of the intervention was estimated. A ratio that greatly favors the 3rd party still has too much impact on war utility, but that would be somewhat difficult to amend, so I hope it'll rarely matter now.
    
    The AI also didn't take into account that, when there are several neighbors that might intervene, those neighbors will themselves have several neighbors whom they could attack instead or whose intervention they fear in turn. I've amended that in the paranoia calculation (that feeds into both the Alert strategy and war utility).
    
    Lastly, the intervention probabilities (derived by UWAI from the paranoia values) were a bit high.
    
    Let's hope that these changes won't decrease the impact of looming interventions in typical midgame/ late-game situations much (still to be tested).

commit 55bfda095dc15b5ac8e31526a69c1633da708b86
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Nov 19 23:07:51 2022 +0100

    Air Bomb mission can hit routes
    
    Inspired by this Close to Home commit:
    https://github.com/Charriu84/CloseToHome/commit/53972be23ca7be372f5e5c7ed7028cd866b32090
    
    ... but I've turned it into a lot more work. I've added XML tags to Civ4RouteInfos.xml that correspond to the AirBombDefense and PillageImprovement BtS tags for improvements. That is, Air Bomb missions against routes aren't guaranteed to succeed, and a bombed (or, to be consistent, pillaged) Railroad is downgraded to a Road. This was pretty straightforward to implement. [advc.255]
    
    Then, there's the question whether routes or improvements should be hit first. I had already made a change - [advc.011] - that lets the tile owner pillage routes before improvements. I've generalized that to apply to air bombardment. (CvUnit::getDestructibleStructure)
    
    And respecting the Fog of War is a recurrent challenge with air missions. I've rewritten part of change [advc.004c] to integrate it with the new route bombing code.
    
    And some related refactoring along the way to make the new code less unwieldy.

commit 7522327e8b80868e02308cf13913fcfe93e74b07
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Nov 12 23:26:13 2022 +0100

    Update AI attitude cache upon war successes
    
    Needed for WarAttitude [advc.sha] and ShareWarAttitude [advc.130m]. To save time, the update is only performed during human turns.
    ExpansionistAttitude and RivalVassalAttitude [advc.130w] are based on power ratios. Rather than update them each time that a power value changes (can happen through population changes, acquired tech, combat ...), the power ratio component of the attitude formula is now cached separately and updated once per turn and upon the conquest of a city. So this change doesn't actually result in the attitude cache being more up to date, but it should avoid failed assertions upon generating attitude breakdowns (help text). Those failed assertions kept getting reported by other modders and might obscure other issues with the attitude cache.

commit c4e93ab9e77ab2b2b26162ace2884fc4a301f1ec
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Oct 30 22:27:35 2022 +0100

    Dial down K-Mod adjustment to espionage mission costs
    
    The K-Mod formula had made the espionage points spent sometimes almost irrelevant for mission costs when one civ had far less population than the other. The result of this, I believe, was a significantly increased frequency of malicious missions against large civs that had conquered some of their neighbors partially. [advc.120k]
    
    Related CFC post (under "Espionage"):
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/advanced-civ.614217/page-53#post-16292755
    and also:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/advanced-civ-play-along-game.678551/page-3#post-16331831

commit 5edc17e477d32835d5d3fea7046fa95202ba5f6a
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Oct 30 22:20:09 2022 +0100

    AI considers HR effect when canceling luxury trades
    
    To address (at least one variety of) rare problems with AI civs canceling resource trades and immediately agreeing to a new trade with the exact same conditions. In the game state I had encountered, the AI was gaining 5 happiness from resources through 3 local luxuries, imported Spice and Hereditary Rule (with the AdvCiv effect of +25% happiness from luxuries). When making the deal, HR was not - and is still not - taken into account; when deciding to cancel the deal, the AI had assumed that it would lose only 1 happiness, not 2. This last part isn't entirely fixed - I'd rather not get into the weeds of anticipating how the HR effect gets rounded in each city -, but the issue should at least come up (even) more rarely now. [advc.912c]

commit 84dfdfe1a533748359b22b2a4bf7d93db1e70f8b
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Oct 30 22:08:44 2022 +0100

    Amends commit
    b506b4e0797ac7dc3bae5be7509abdd8cb54d72f
    
    In cases when the initial search for trade items to offer for peace came up empty, the second part (AI_counterPropose) wasn't executed, resulting in a square peace deal being offered. (Instead, the AI should offer what little it has or not make an offer at all.) [advc.134a]
    
    (I've only tested an earlier version of this bugfix; let's hope that this final version still does the job.)

commit 5559fcb2f10d53270605e1201b99de3508cee714
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Oct 28 17:50:06 2022 +0200

    Allow revolts during occupation even when at war
    
    [change id advc.023]
    
    Foreign culture strength gets halved under occupation. Previously, AdvCiv had halved the revolt probability during occupation - which doesn't make it any easier to bring that probability all the way down to 0 -, and flipping was impossible when at war. This change should mean that revolts in quick succession (before the previous revolt has even been pacified) will only affect cities that are substantially under-garrisoned.
    
    When at war, foreign culture strength is halved (pretty much how it was in BtS), and when both at war and under occupation (e.g. when a city has just been conquered), these effects multiply, so foreign culture strength is quartered. This means it's no longer possible to leave newly conquered cities in a state of perpetual revolt, but keeping them from revolting (or at least from flipping while the war is still being fought) should only require modest garrisons.
    
    Lastly, and I already regret this part, a city without any garrison that revolts while in occupation and at war flips immediately and even if no enemy cities are nearby. This seems plausible, but complicates things even further for too little gain.
    
    Related CFC post (paragraph that starts with "Keeping Boudica alive", somewhere in the middle):
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/advanced-civ-play-along-game.678551/post-16330837

commit e376e2f78e2d33f5d397c476e9ed9bd2f8d58091

commit 6ccb1c47dad0b7286f0d1859cce3600cb0108123

    Plot needs to be adj. to two rivers to connect their trade

commit 82e67788d9bc1e7f2ba47bd317cd444c28a57f19
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Aug 31 19:20:54 2022 +0200

    Don't show red waypoint for attack when out of moves
    
    More specifically, when a unit has already attacked, BtS will indicate that further attacks are illegal through a red waypoint. This is misleading when the target of the attack can't be reached on the current turn - because, by the time that the attacker gets there, it will again be able to attack. My fix only addresses the (typical) case in which the attacker has spent all its moves. (Because this case is simple - no target can then be reached on the current turn, so no red waypoint should be shown for any target. [advc.004]

commit ef2ec4be8cb9741afeb32a00128faa3092fd3ecf
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Aug 31 19:15:09 2022 +0200

    Minor refactor in calculateResearchModifier

commit f3094bb391cd63d1a8e5e78160f39b937d4c3190
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Mon Aug 22 19:34:20 2022 +0200

    Faster ScaledNum::mulDiv for size(IntType) < 4
    
    Currently, IntType is pretty much always int, so this is only for possible future uses. Specifically, I've been thinking about how the combat odds calculation would have to be changed if there were a combat round limit. Fast exponentiation of fixed-point probabilities could then matter, and 2-byte precision would (likely) suffice.
    
    (Speeding things up for 4 byte would be trickier; would have to look into intrinsics.)
    
    Also fixed some compilation issue for IntType = unsigned short.

    Reorder unit command buttons, use two rows.
    
    [change id advc.004k]
    
    More or less swapped the position of misc. missions and commands (but the important ones have an "order priority set explicitly through XML) and moved promotions and upgrades to the very (right) end and, if there is space, into a separate row.

commit 350c2483a7ea68ef52d267357bdb1f5c135f549b
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Jul 2 21:23:24 2022 +0200

    Partly restore BtS behavior for choice of "center unit"
    
    Units with available moves are - again - preferred as the center unit of a tile, i.e. the unit that gets shown on the map and - as I've realized through this CFC post
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/advanced-civ.614217/page-52#post-16278294
    - the unit that gets selected when a tile is clicked.
    
    I had disabled the available-moves condition as part of a bugfix: karadoc had intended to disable that condition, according to a comment, but he had accidentally disabled a different one instead.
    
    Now available moves are checked again, but only during the active (human) player's turn. That should be the best of both worlds, but could also be confusing when a center unit changes upon ending a turn. Let's see.
    
    I've also refactored the calls to getBestDefender to avoid passing half a dozen bool parameters.

commit 5355820f3ac6530a945b4267323cfcdb532b0d0e
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Jun 29 19:27:32 2022 +0200

    Accept replays created by the Taurus mod
    
    ... when HOF_DISPLAY_OTHER_MOD_REPLAYS is set in XML. Taurus sets a particular bit in its replay version number - to be able to identify its own replays even when the mod name isn't stored in the replay file. AdvCiv generally assumes that replays of other mods are incompatible when the replay version number has been increased. But, in the case of Taurus, which is essentially BULL, there is no actual problem with compatibility. [advc.106i]

commit ce4a94c922cfcf8b34a0dd4c3fce4097106afa37
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Jun 29 18:24:55 2022 +0200

    Fix nextNonDefault functions of ListEnumMap
    
    [change id: advc.enum]
    
    Default values can be (explicitly) stored in a ListEnumMap, namely, when a key is reset to the default value after having previously been set to a nondefault value. ListEnumMap will not remove the key-value pair in that situation. Therefore, the nextNonDefault functions need to filter out nondefault values.
    
    These comparisons are unnecessary, however, when a ListEnumMap has a monotony property: values only ever change from default to nondefault - unless all keys are reset at once, clearing the map. So I've added a new class template "NonDefaultEnumMap", derived from ListEnumMap for all data loaded from XML - which has the monotony property.
    
    The way that nextNonDefault has been used thus far, there hasn't been any problem (I think), but the old behavior of returning default values from nextNonDefault could've easily lead to problems in the future.
    
    Related CFC post (last paragraph):
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/question-about-cvplot-cpp-mod-with-arrays.677378/#post-16290351

commit 42c987073f06a4b07f1dc2234a12a75a0787c425
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun May 8 23:09:54 2022 +0200

    Make plot indicator runtime patch more robust
    
    [change id advc.092b]
    
    By falling back on a search for the appropriate region of the Civ4BeyondSword.exe code section when an instruction isn't found where the patch expects it. In case that e.g. localized editions of the game merely require a small offset to virtual addresses to be patched successfully. But I only have access to the MULTI5 version, so I don't know if this will accomplish anything.
    
    And memory protections of the OS are now restored after the patch. They're, in principle, helpful for catching bugs, and turning the protections back on may also reduce the risk of being mistaken for a virus at runtime. (As for static virus checks, I've uploaded the DLL to VirusTotal.com now; no problems reported there. Apparently, just having VirtualProtect calls in the code does not raise suspicion.)
    
    DLL updated (Assert build)

commit 91e1f2153a6e0adbbe6bfae88a9a0dae41f28b0b
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun May 8 01:19:44 2022 +0200

    Some tweaks to camera behavior
    
    Through GlobalDefines that I had not been aware of previously. [advc.004m]
    
    Increased camera scroll speed, i.e. faster movement parallel to the ground when pressing the arrow keys or when moving the mouse cursor to an edge of the screen. Related CFC thread:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/trying-to-edit-scrollspeed-but-no-luck-any-idéas.674976
    
    Camera distance on the city screen gets (slightly) adjusted to the field-of-view value. Can avoid issues like in this thread
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/city-map-zoom.676680/
    that way.
    
    Slightly steeper camera angle (more top-down). And slightly bigger field of view by default. Because the flatter camera angle that tends to result from a bigger field of view (player likely to zoom in a little farther) gets evened out by the direct change to the camera angle - and because the impact of the field of view on the size ratio between plots and plot indicators (balloons) is no longer a concern.

commit 5d0207b04f3ede3addc443ef19f6835a0f2c4c09
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Mon Mar 14 22:44:47 2022 +0100

    Overhauled the years-per-turn progression
    
    [change id advc.910]
    
    Can't keep increasing tech costs whenever the AI becomes more effective. In this instance, the cause of expedited AI research is probably either the recent bugfix in the AI eval of tech paths
    a221c7efc5e89f97d3ab18286efe9ab646fb5907
    or changes to UWAI that may avoid some inconclusive warfare or war preparations. (Or a bit of both.)
    Anyway, I've looked at tech discovery dates in some sample games to come up with desired associations of turn numbers with game years, and then (with the help of an Excel sheet) tweaked the game speed data to match those dates. This has, predictably, resulted in longer periods of the smallest time-per-turn increments at the end of the game. For example, on Normal speed, 6 months per turn are now counted already starting on turn 348 (was turn 430).
    
    Another aim has been to bring down the date of the earliest wars between civs. Doesn't feel like ancient warfare when the game year already approaches AD 1, even if the technology is still pre-Medieval.

commit e285df81a5d469271321b806ba65b05a3b7b494e
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Mar 12 22:42:03 2022 +0100

    Finer scale for cell grids of map scripts
    
    Previously, maps had consisted of cells of 4x4 tiles. Therefore, width and height had to be multiples of 4, and that made it difficult to fine-tune map sizes. Now width and height are multiples of 2. Graphically, CvLandscapeInfos still defines cells as 4x4 tiles, but width and height no longer conform to that format. I don't see any graphical artifacts caused by this change. [advc.137]
    
    Any maps that override getGridSize - i.e. most maps that aren't included in AdvCiv - still use multiples of 4. The maps included in AdvCiv now use a new function "getNumPlotsPercent" for size adjustment - and no longer override getGridSize. [advc.165]
    
    Aspect ratios are still ca. 1.4, and tend to be lower for small map size and higher for large map size (because tropics and polar zone being close together is more of a problem on smaller sizes). I intend to keep these aspect ratios (hadn't been sure previously).

    Also turns out that I had overlooked the getGridSize function already defined by the original Pangaea script. Therefore, my earlier attempts at adjusting the grid size of that script had had no effect. [advc.165]

    Fractal maps: choose smarter internal dimensions
    
    The height maps generated by the Fractal algo normally use a 2:1 aspect ratio. Ought to be better to use 1:1 when the map dimensions are closer to that ratio. commit e53bde3abca5c94e51b5538f2a0cc5582c5fe2fd
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Feb 23 23:35:03 2022 +0100

    Overhaul AI eval of religion techs
    
    [change id advc.171]
    
    For the three early religions: Reduce the impact of randomness, turn number and city count and instead consider happiness needed in cities (i.e. in the capital) and the need for border expansion (in the 2nd city, though the capital will also help). As a result, an AI civ will usually go for a religion tech around the time that it founds a 2nd city. On average, this seems to be around the same time as in K-Mod (which founds religions a good deal later than BtS).
    
    I've increased the impact of the urgency created by one or two of the early religion having already been taken. This should make it harder for a human player to found all three.
    
    Flavor is still a big factor, and favorite religion arguably a bit more important than in K-Mod. (Seems to have had fairly little impact.)
    
    For the later religions, I've mostly kept the K-Mod logic. Now trying harder to avoid founding a non-favorite religion, especially: not to be motivated by the favorite religion if getting there will likely result in founding another religion first. This is mainly relevant for the Abrahamic religions I think.
    
    (I'll move the code into a subroutine in a separate commit.)

commit a91cee293923370002503e95b41831c42d74d42f
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Feb 18 14:52:41 2022 +0100

    Re-enable worker stealing - with new restrictions
    
    To wit: 50% chance that the worker is destroyed rather than stolen, 100% on the turn that war is declared. Combat help shows the chance. [advc.010]
    I.e. will usually be able to steal workers (or settlers) only upon conquering cities. And AI cities may scrap workers (ca. 25% chance) when they're all but certain to be conquered on the next turn. The main point of re-enabling worker stealing at all is that it seems strange (or disquieting) that no civilian units ever survive combat. And I guess some few free workers when conquering a large swath of land are convenient to have (w/o having too much impact on game balance). And, previously, there was no incentive at all for attacking (rarely occurring) orphaned workers (no city to retreat to).
    
    CFC thread with previous discussions about unlocking worker stealing through a tech (3rd quote box):
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/k-mod-far-beyond-the-sword.407049/page-151#post-15822719
    (I've also considered a capture chance based on the distance to nearest tile owned by the captor - rather than a flat 0% chance upon  declaring war. That would feel more organic, but is also more complex and can still result in early high-stakes gambles when two civs start close together.
    Getting the AI to protect its workers better is too much effort. I've written some code, but I'll archive that away on a separate branch.)

    Decrease AnimalAttackProb (except on Settler difficulty)
    
    Now 70% rather than 90% on most difficulty levels. Mainly to make the animals' behavior appear a little more natural, and to make it so that players who want the animal to attack may have to stalk it a little bit. I guess I'd prefer a probability closer to 50%, but I don't want players to worry too much about this change (and the whole animal thing is still pretty terrible either way). [advc.309]

commit cb0d876f2db705aed3e27b17892da1caf53634a2
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Feb 15 23:27:26 2022 +0100

    Tweaks to base Barbarian creation rate
    
    Slightly fewer animals (except on low difficulty levels) [advc.309], slightly more non-Animal Barbarians [advc.300].
    
    Had already decreased the Animal rate at an earlier time. I don't agree that animals should become a lot more common on the high difficulty levels. Gives this rather silly element of the game (mainly good for teaching combat to beginners and to make the world seem more alive) too much importance, and I think experienced players don't appreciate randomly losing their starting units.

[advc.tsl, advc.701]

    DarkLunaPhantom/Kek-Mod@908160ecea97d427cc24736fb4fb1e1b51f282f3
    which describes a similar problem with the Random Leader Personalities option.

Date:   Sun Dec 12 22:59:22 2021 +0100

    PerfectMongoose: Tweaks to plate tectonics params
    
    Increased the distanceFilterSize parameter. Don't know what the effect is exactly, but this appears to lead to somewhat bulkier continents. It's the main difference that I'm able to see between the PerfectMongoose PW2 and Totestra land generators. (Apart from that, Totestra probably generates bigger continents mainly through bigger map dimensions and a higher land-sea ratio.) For variety, I'm randomizing the distanceFilterSize, and also the plateGrowthChance - another parameter relevant for continent size. [advc.021b]

commit efe76e5917516f0c8a7e96b2601d66d318459426
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>

    AI: Don't adopt Space3/4 strat without any SS parts
    
    Ensure that a substantial portion of the needed Spaceship parts have been produced before switching to stage 3 or 4 of the Space victory strategy. BBAI/K-Mod had only required sufficient tech progress. Important not to switch to stage 3 or 4 of any victory strategy too early because UWAI looks at those stages to determine which rival civs are on track to victory. [advc.115]

commit e658c45fb936df8458c34f67e305f2e166fd23e9
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Dec 2 00:58:01 2021 +0100

    Redistribute AI weight for unavailable victory strats
    
    So that AI leaders will e.g. be more inclined to focus on Culture victory early when Space victory is disabled. The non-applicable weights are distributed according to the positive weights of the valid victory conditions; i.e. an AI leader who normally isn't at all interested in the Culture victory strategy, still won't become interested when Space victory is taken away. [advc.115f]
    
    I think there were also some minor issues in UWAI and R&F code with assumptions about human victory strategies. Such assumptions shouldn't be affected by the preferred victory strategies of AI leaders played by humans. Cleaned up: the AI now assumes that human players give every valid victory condition the same weight (of 30), regardless of the leader personality.
    
    And for mod-mods: Can now set negative AI weights in XML to prevent particular leaders from pursuing certain victory strategies at all -- 0 weight didn't and doesn't have that effect. (Regardless of AI weights, any leader can still stumble onto any victory condition.)

commit 32857921420d2fcd21120d057501dd245f730a28
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Nov 24 00:06:11 2021 +0100

    Decrease Pangaea map dimensions a little bit
    
    For all world size settings, reverting commit
    5d751ff409bb2d5909f980830e49b49acc1c8764
    in the process. [advc.165]
    
    While the previous dimensions had been closer to giving Pangaea maps the same number of bonus resources as Fractal and Continents, all land being immediately accessible means (arguably) that there should be slightly fewer resources (and thus slightly fewer city sites) overall. Despite some tweaks to the UWAI component, there was no warfare before the Medieval era in about half of my test games on the Standard world size (with 8 civs). Having looked at those games from the perspective of each civ, I think the AI was mostly correct in not starting any wars. Perhaps the map was just a little too spacious; the tests look better now.

commit f39e13df870c036c2e5d0db26437254760898bdf
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Nov 19 23:31:13 2021 +0100

    Add ThirdPartyIntervention war utility aspect
    
    I.e. decrease the utility of waging war when fearing an intervention by a dangerous third party. In part based on code I had written 4 years ago and shelved because I had worried that such AI behavior would make stalemates too common. Since then, I've often found it painful to watch the AI walk into predictable and devastating two-front wars. I think I've made pretty sure that the AI will only fear actual threats; stalemates don't look like a problem in my tests. There also tends to be rather too much warfare in the late game; won't hurt to put a bit of a brake on that.
    
    Also makes use of the "paranoia" calculation that was previously only used for the "Alert" AI strategy. I've tweaked that calculation a bit. [advc.022]

commit 3bb274cbdcccff34241ae0bf6e2526fe0fb106db
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Nov 19 03:48:26 2021 +0100

    UWAI: Don't plan war against faraway member of a DP

commit 1b796618e77be46b120f77413c20ff6bf187bdba
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Nov 19 03:45:14 2021 +0100

    UWAI: Predict distraction by war allies more accurately
    
    When simulating a clash between two armies, the distraction caused by third war parties had overestimated third parties expected to attack lightly defended cities. A border city with a high defensive modifier may indeed easily hold off a third party, but this logic mustn't be applied when it comes to the predicted sizes of garrisons: when a city is expected to be lightly manned, then it's probably an unimportant city and an attack won't cause more distraction than an attack against a more important city would.
    
    As a result, multiple weak civs had often been too confident about defeating a single strong civ, and the strong civ wasn't confident enough.

    Progressive unit production discounts (based on the game turn through change advc.251; originally based on player era) are now also taken into account, i.e. on high difficulty levels, the AI assembles bigger stacks as the game progresses. (That was already the case through code that looks at era numbers - but now even more so and especially on the highest difficulty levels.) [advc.104p]

commit 7d188442558925b31b862948b1148b1cd1854447
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Nov 13 03:05:48 2021 +0100

    Replace recently added kludges for higher war utility
    
    Fully reverts commit
    787f3338131f8f705e78fe4362efe55069cfa8ad
    
    The bugfixes in the previous commit have already done far more than those tweaks to make the AI more bellicose. Still, I think the evaluation of potential post-war uses of units trained for a war should be tweaked a bit further. And the bugfixes haven't specifically made the AI more willing to conclude war preparations in the early game; that's still a problem (had been a problem even before I introduced those bugs). A better solution will be to increase the impact of war preparations on AI city production choices a bit; I'll do that too. But war utility can also be tweaked a little; could mean that early AI wars will more often fail to achieve their objectives, but that's still better than no action before the common era.

commit d1d30e2d5c32771b249291d352106b771b251202
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Nov 13 02:43:08 2021 +0100

    Fix UWAI bugs that had made the AI too peaceable
    
    Two of these were introduced by the stylistic overhaul in v1.00:
    ee0ddea124b64cc8e18f5e29ad693d81b5298545
    
    A variable had not been reset in between evaluating the diplomatic ill will from a potential war enemy and its partners. This had caused the costs for ill will to be counted multiple times. Except in situations when relations with the target were already spoiled, this had made the AI far more reluctant to start wars than it should've been.
    
    Utility for reparations had been counted even when neither side was expected to lose cities, in particular also in the peace scenario. Since the total utility of a war plan is the difference between the war and peace scenario, possible reparations had effectively not been taken into account and war utility was a bit lower than it should have been in many situations.
    
    The last bug was that UWAI had ignored the time horizon of a simulated war when estimating how much the military power of civs not involved in the war will increase. It had instead always done a 10-turn projection and thus underestimated the military power of those civs and therefore also underestimated the post-war utility of units produced for a war. On the bottom line, militarily powerful civs had tended to (not dramatically, but significantly) overestimate the opportunity cost of starting a war. I think this oversight had existed since the initial release of the mod.

commit 787f3338131f8f705e78fe4362efe55069cfa8ad

commit 8ac818c755148af30ba928d1d26f3140e2d3fc45
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Nov 6 20:48:07 2021 +0100

    AI more reluctant to throttle military production
    
    ... when more powerful than all potential enemies. I think my original change was too stark. It had caused the AI to gradually reduce its build-unit probability as soon as it was militarily ahead of all potential enemies. I'd say the reduction started to have a noticeable effect when 50% ahead. This may have seriously impeded the ability of the AI to win a military victory. Doing that efficiently requires an overwhelming military advantage (considering also that large empires have a lot of military power tied down as garrisons). Now the adjustment only starts when the AI is at least 25% ahead, i.e. it should become noticeable when about 75% ahead. When pursuing a military victory strategy, this buffer is further increased. [advc.017]

commit da67f921a75e46b049f792da01f1a3cbfdde904e
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Nov 6 20:36:26 2021 +0100

    Tweaks to AI evaluation of tech trades
    
    Increase the impact of the utility that the AI assigns to techs that it receives (or that it'll impart to another AI civ). Previously, at most one third of the overall trade value had been subtracted when a tech had low utility, now up to 42% can be subtracted. And can add up to 27.5% (instead of 25%) when utility is high. [advc.550g]
    
    Reduce early-game discounts for weak civs (score of known techs, military power level) in tech trades. [advc.550a]
    
    Both changes are intended to make "trade bait" less powerful on the highest difficulty levels. Should e.g. no longer be possible to trade Aesthetics (which the AI will rarely prioritize - because it's not useful early on) 1-for-1 for Alphabet or Mathematics -- unless the recipient is actually somewhat keen on Aesthetics.
    
    Not going to accomplish a great deal I think; Aesthetics and Compass (through a Great Scientist) are still going to be powerful - and often crucial - early techs on Immortal and Deity. Hopefully, things will at least no longer be worse than in BtS.

    Typedef CvInfo base classes for easier use of CvXMLInfo
    
    I don't want to derive all the CvInfo classes from CvXMLInfo so long as they don't make use of the addElements function - because CvXMLInfo adds 24 byte of memory per instance (for two std::vectors). I do want to make it easier for mod-mods to change a base class to CvXMLInfo. That can now be done in a single place in the header file. The references to the base class in the implementation files now use the base class typedef from the header. [advc.tag]

commit 4be30af01caf1ffefd832c6ee4dea66bd290456e
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Oct 12 20:50:51 2021 +0200

    Streamline religion, civic AI diplo adjustments
    
    The different-religion penalty now starts at -1 (or -2 with the Holy City) for all AI leaders. For the majority of the leaders, the penalty then becomes one worse after 15 turns and, for some of the leaders, another one worse after another 15 turns. The total limits remain the same for all leaders. This is the same principle as for the same-religion and same-civic modifiers (but those increase every 10 turns and, overall, can grow bigger than the different-religion penalties).
    
    Previously, different-religion penalties had started at 0 to -2 (another -1 with the Holy City) and had then grown one worse after 5 turns.
    
    Now that all three ideological modifiers (same/ different religion, same civic) have a small constant portion and a larger time-based portion, the time-based portions are all essentially given the same adjustment to the popularity of the ideology, specifically the number of cities of known civs with the ideology in question. [advc.130n]
    
    This obsoletes change [advc.130x] which had adjusted the different-religion penalty based on the population sizes of known cities with the two religions in question. Change id 130x instead refers to the following accompanying change now: Each time that a time-based ideological modifier increases, the time for the next increase is incremented by one turn.
    
    This commit also takes care of attitude cache updates after loading older savegames -- which are also needed for additions to change [advc.148] previously committed.
    
    Related CFC post (1st spoiler box):
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/advanced-civ.614217/page-50#post-16165134

    Reduce shared-civic diplo for half of the leaders
    
    Namely for everyone with a FavoriteCivicAttitudeChangeLimit of 4 or greater except Lincoln, Mansa Musa, Washington and Willem. By exempting those four (which all have a limit of 4), I end up reducing the limit of almost exactly half of the AI leaders. The limits get reduced by 1 point. [advc.148]
    
    Note that the limit does not include the flat (not time-based) +1 relations from FavoriteCivicAttitudeChange.

commit 3a25964b7fd503d8b5c3c098d482f26cd401084d

    Reduce shared-religion diplo for half of the leaders
    
    Namely for all leaders with a SameReligionAttitudeChangeLimit of 5 or greater (this also includes all leaders with a favorite civic that implies a state religion) and for about half of those with a limit of 4. I've reduced the limits by 1 point. [advc.148]

commit b1128b818abf4d3763ae8c297a313f70da8f22f4
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Sep 23 00:16:15 2021 +0200

    R&F: Increase player handicap beyond game handicap
    
    I.e. use a handicap one level higher than the game handicap (set on the Custom Game screen) for the current human civ and Prince (instead of Noble) for all AI civs. This should increase expenses (for all civs) while leaving the challenge of competing against the AI civs and Barbarians essentially the same (i.e. as one would expect from the game handicap). The underlying assumption is that R&F games are played at a several levels lower difficulty than non-R&F games; expenses can then feel like a nonfactor. [advc.708]
    
    Also increase expenses on medium difficulty levels - mainly for the same reasons as stated above, but not just for R&F games. [advc.251]

commit 40060514c0e678c1d2bd252c961eef0e1333121b
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Mon Aug 30 20:18:08 2021 +0200

    Simplify accesses to CvInitCore::m_eActivePlayer
    
    I didn't want to put a getActivePlayer function in the global namespace, so I've instead added free getActivePlayer functions to a few implementation files where they are frequently needed. Likewise getActiveTeam. I've also added boolean functions isActive to CvPlayer and CvTeam and isActiveOwned and isActiveTeam to CvPlot, CvCity, CvUnit and CvSelectionGroup. To allow those functions to be inlined without additional header-in-header inclusions and without whole-program optimization, CvInitCore (whose header gets precompiled and is therefore included everywhere) now caches the active team id in addition to the active player id.

commit dbd409affe05e8efd7b6c86d77b65d2f3e4a5535
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Aug 29 22:32:26 2021 +0200

    Group pathfinder prefers landing on routes
    
    [change id advc.pf]
    
    When breaking ties between paths of equal length, paths that end on a tile with a route are now preferred. And AI units now have the same preference (i.e. only a slight one) for diagonal moves as human players. This gives other tiebreakers (including the one based on routes) greater importance.
    
    Apart from yielding, in my estimation, slightly better paths, this change also works around a rare issue that can cause valid paths to be ruled out when avoiding dangerous tiles. The specific situation seems worth documenting:
    
    I've gotten an AI worker trying to retreat toward a city stuck in a loop because the clean pathfinder instance in CvSelectionGroup::groupPathTo did not find any valid path whereas the pathfinder call in CvUnitAI::AI_retreatToCity did find one with the help of data cached from previous calls. ASCII art:
    | | | |D
    |A|B|C|
    |H|E| |
    A is the start, D the destination, and B, C and D have a Road; A and E do not. H contains a hostile unit. Due to the diagonal bias (and no bias for moving onto a route), the pathfinder first processed E, and found that entering C from E is not allowed because the worker would then end the turn on a tile threatened by H. This causes the pathfinder to permanently regard C as a dead end, without consideration of the cheaper path via B that allows the worker to reach the safe tile D in a single turn.
    
    It's not correct to let the canStepThrough function ("pathValid_source" in K-Mod) take path data (remaining moves) into consideration. Strictly speaking, danger can't be checked by that function. I guess it could be done in isValidStep ("pathValid_join" in K-Mod), but I expect that this would hurt performance significantly. Not worth it for such a rare problem -- that will become even more rare (impossible?) through my change to the tiebreakers.
    
    This example suggests to me that the route bias may, more generally, help the pathfinder process promising paths first. That might lead to a small gain in performance.

commit 4ee50e1f9072916e2af596935472176b6d83116a
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Aug 24 19:56:23 2021 +0200

    Place Barbarian units based on per-tile weights
    
    Instead of choosing a (valid) tile uniformly at random, a tile is now chosen based on a probability distribution derived from a weight distribution. [advc.304]
    
    Instead of re-rolling nonarable tiles twice, they have 20% weight for being chosen while arable tiles have 100% weight. A tile now counts as arable (in this context) if the minimum of its total natural yield including terrain features and excluding terrain features exceeds 1.5 - with commerce yield being counted as 0.5. Resources count only if they're revealed to the Barbarians. The previous conditions were less clear, had treated Tundra river as arable and had a potential for giving away unrevealed resources. Re-rolling twice had made Barbarians too rare on nonarable tiles when the portion of nonarable tiles among unobserved tiles was small - and not rare enough when that portion was large. [advc.300]
    
    Moreover, the game now remembers on which tiles Barbarian units have been placed or destroyed, and Barbarian placement and movement near such tiles is discouraged (less likely) for a while. [advc.304]
    
    Related CFC post:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/advanced-civ.614217/page-49#post-16139592

commit 8eec729405fd4992a8f429d628d1df0d5fa00c55

commit 59a3e3190061b421b117b58d047aa1196259f5fa
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Aug 17 23:54:46 2021 +0200

    Rewrite of enum map classes
    
    This merges the ArrayEnumMap and ListEnumMap types that I had been using for data loaded from XML (offline problem) with Nightinggale's (array-based) EnumMap ("We the People" mod) that I had been using for data members that change continually (online problem). Now based on a traits system for enum types. [advc.enum, advc.003t]
    
    This rewrite has necessitated a fair number of (non-functional) changes to the XML loading code and to the serialization code - in order to maintain savegame compatibility.
    Enum bounds are now asserted for simple enum values read from XML. [advc.006j]
    
    This commit also fixes a bug in the AdvCiv starting position algorithm: When copying SolutionAttributes instances, the volatilityValues enum map had been omitted. Hard to say how consequential that was; might be a significant improvement to have it fixed. [advc.027]

commit b07af8c2e4bf77488c69daaa83583459512994a3
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Jul 28 00:52:34 2021 +0200

    Tweak Holy City religion spread chance
    
    Increased the spread probability by 25% (not by 25 percentage points!) overall in order to even out a change that [advc.140] had made to the distance calculation.
    
    And added a special clause for civs that still have 0 cities with the Holy City religion: increase the spread probability a little if such civs have fewer cities than the (map-size-based - e.g. 5 on Standard-size maps) target number of cities, and decrease the probability if the city count exceeds the target. This should make the overall chance of a religion spreading to a civ less dependent on its city count. [advc.173]

    While AI civs that lack Copper and Horse are very keen on researching Iron Working early on, I've lately seen the bulk of the AI civs delay Iron Working into the late Classical era. Not sure if I had been too focused on the early adopters in earlier tests - or if I've made some AI tweak elsewhere that has made the AI less interested in Iron Working.

commit f3224a8a3245ae097c4317843137f855e9585b27
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Jul 14 21:02:04 2021 +0200

    More culture rate tweaks
    
    Reverted K-Mod decreases of wonder culture: [advc.200]
    Pyramids, Hanging Gardens, Colossus, Chichen Itza: 5 -> 6
    Great Library, Angkor Wat, Hagia Sophia, Spiral Minaret, University of Sankore, Shwedagon Paya 6 -> 8
    Notre Dame, Taj Mahal: 8 -> 10
    Creative Constructions (not a wonder): 2.5 -> 3.0 per resource
    
    Set to 0 for the sake of simplicity: [advc.201]
    National Park: 3 -> 0
    Red Cross: 2 -> 0
    all Corporate Headquarters: 2 -> 0
    
    Cristo Redentor: 5 -> 6 [advc.201]
    To match Statue of Liberty.
    
    Great Wall: 2 -> 4 [advc.310]
    Doesn't need to have an unusually low culture rate; AdvCiv makes drastic changes to this wonder anyway, changing the culture rate won't make the changes more complex overall. (But a high culture rate would contribute to the wall graphic not matching the cultural borders before long.)
    
    Sistine Chapel: 7 -> 8
    Restoring the K-Mod value; I had recently
    30c5da13136cc6263c3cb4024090638c179471f8
    reduced it by 1 further - it was 10 in BtS.
    
    The only K-Mod decreases of wonder culture that I haven't (fully) reverted concern Stonehenge, Temple of Artemis, Oracle, Great Lighthouse, Parthenon, Statue of Zeus, Mausoleum of Maussolos, Sistine Chapel. I.e. mostly wonders that produce a lot of culture in the early game. I suppose such buildings are indeed a bit problematic wrt. the K-Mod culture spread changes.

commit 408f57c58141e952bf09fd57ce1d3f3855042022
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Jul 9 16:25:37 2021 +0200

    Cache plot index at CvPlot
    
    Letting CvMap compute the index takes a multiplication and an addition (multiplicand and addend being unknown at compile time), and it's unnecessarily verbose when the CvPlot instance is already at hand. Should be worth the 2 extra byte (which were taken up by padding anyway). [advc.opt]
    
    And revert a list-based enum map back to an array-based one: access to revealed routes needs to be fast for pathfinding. [advc.enum]

commit b5167e6306eb28195edf799d5cf1ea80a25573a7
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Jul 9 00:01:52 2021 +0200

    Remove most inline keywords
    
    [change id advc.inl]
    
    The keywords are nice for making the reader aware that a function is very frequently called, but I don't think it's ultimately worth the clutter, and as for performance ... Maybe I'll compare once I've put together this commit. I'm pretty sure that there's not much of a difference, but I've made other changes along the way, so it's difficult to say right now.
    
    I've also removed inline keywords that (I think) standard C++ would require for the one-definition rule, but that are dispensable in MSVC03. Seems to be that function templates and members of class templates never need an inline keyword.
    
    Where "inline" is not required by the linker, "__inline" is now preferred; for clarity.
    
    For free functions, I still use __inline a lot so that even debug builds - through the Ob1 compiler option - can inline them. (Apparently, the Ob1 option can always inline member functions defined in a class definition, but, elsewhere, an inline keyword is required. That's also what the VS documentation says.)
    
    And I'm removing some of the "...External" counterparts of inline functions. (The ones I'm keeping exist because of some signature change; not to avoid exported inline functions.)
